{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_012LJcRCRpx9m2LqZGHFtUYa","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # `client-go` Architecture\\n2: \\n3: This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. It describes the\\n4: major components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.\\n5: \\n6: ## Client Configuration\\n7: \\n8: There is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The\\n9: `rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The\\n10: `tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the\\n11: complex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external\\n12: authentication providers (e.g., OIDC).\\n13: \\n14: ## REST Client\\n15: \\n16: The `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates\\n17: the low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,\\n18: Kubernetes-specific object logic.\\n19: \\n20: The `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a\\n21: chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. Each element in the chain is responsible for a specific\\n22: task, such as adding an `Authorization` header. This is the mechanism by which all authentication\\n23: is injected into requests.\\n24: \\n25: The client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring\\n26: response processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to\\n27: supporting different client models from a common base.\\n28: \\n29: ### Endpoint Interactions\\n30: \\n31: *   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format\\n32:     (JSON or Protobuf). A key performance optimization using this mechanism is the ability to\\n33:     request metadata-only objects via the `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameter.\\n34:     Also the `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameters may be used to request lists as tables. \\n35: *   **Subresources:** The client can target standard subresources like `/status` or `/scale` for\\n36:     object mutations, and it can also handle action-oriented subresources like `/logs` or\\n37:     `/exec`, which often involve streaming data.\\n38: *   **List Pagination:** For `LIST` requests, the client can specify a `limit`. The server will\\n39:     return up to that many items and, if more exist, a `continue` token. The client is\\n40:     responsible for passing this token in a subsequent request to retrieve the next page.\\n41:     Higher-level tools like the `Reflector`'s `ListerWatcher` handle this logic automatically.\\n42: *   **Streaming Watches:** A `WATCH` request returns a `watch.Interface` (from\\n43:     `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch`), which provides a channel of structured `watch.Event`\\n44:     objects (`ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, `BOOKMARK`). This decouples the watch consumer from\\n45:     the underlying streaming protocol.\\n46: \\n47: ### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\\n48: \\n49: *   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\\n50:     `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\\n51: *   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\\n52:     `WarningHandler`.\\n53: *   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\\n54:     client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\\n55: *   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\\n56:     responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\\n57: \\n58: ## Typed and Dynamic Clients\\n59: \\n60: To handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\\n61: models.\\n62: \\n63: The **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\\n64: \\n65: The **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\\n66: to interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\\n67: 1.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\\n68:     **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\\n69: 2.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\\n70:     resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\\n71: \\n72: ## Code Generation\\n73: \\n74: A core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\\n75: strongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\\n76: controller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\\n77: several key components:\\n78: \\n79: *   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\\n80: *   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\\n81: *   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\\n82: *   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\\n83: \\n84: A contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\\n85: of these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\\n86: \\n87: `sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\\n88: \\n89: ## Controller Infrastructure\\n90: \\n91: The `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\\n92: request-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\\n93: \\n94: The data flow is as follows:\\n95: \\n96: ```mermaid\\n97: graph TD\\n98:     subgraph \\\"Kubernetes API\\\"\\n99:         API_Server[API Server]\\n100:     end\\n101: \\n102:     subgraph \\\"client-go: Informer Mechanism\\\"\\n103:         Reflector(\\\"1. Reflector\\\")\\n104:         DeltaFIFO(\\\"2. DeltaFIFO\\\")\\n105:         Indexer[\\\"3. Indexer (Cache)\\\"]\\n106:         EventHandlers(\\\"4. Event Handlers\\\")\\n107:     end\\n108: \\n109:     subgraph \\\"User Code\\\"\\n110:         WorkQueue[\\\"5. Work Queue\\\"]\\n111:         Controller(\\\"6. Controller\\\")\\n112:     end\\n113: \\n114:     API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\\n115:     Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\\n116:     DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\\n117:     Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\\n118:     EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\\n119:     WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\\n120:     Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\\n121: ```\\n122: \\n123: A **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\\n124: `resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\\n125: stream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\\n126: **\\\"too old\\\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\\n127: `Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\\n128: `resourceVersion` to restart from.\\n129: \\n130: The **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\\n131: logic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\\n132: \\n133: ## Controller Patterns\\n134: \\n135: The controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\\n136: ensure resiliency.\\n137: \\n138: The **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\\n139: and reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\\n140: work queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\\n141: blocking the informer's watch stream.\\n142: \\n143: For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\\n144: solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\\n145: shared `Lease` object.\\n146: \\n147: ## Server-Side Apply\\n148: \\n149: `client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\\n150: server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\\n151: model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\\n152: **`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\\n153: construct the declarative patch.\\n154: \\n155: ## Versioning and Compatibility\\n156: \\n157: `client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\\n158: version `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\\n159: \\n160: The Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\\n161: version of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\\n162: A contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\\n163: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2be44042-0639-40cf-99c5-188f09ad71df","uuid":"24257837-9fa3-4353-a71d-38512de78f36","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # `client-go` Architecture\\n2: \\n3: This document explains the internal architecture of `client-go` for contributors. It describes the\n4: major components, how they interact, and the key design decisions that shape the library.\n5: \n6: ## Client Configuration\n7: \n8: There is an architectural separation between loading client configuration and using it. The\n9: `rest.Config` object is the in-memory representation of this configuration. The\n10: `tools/clientcmd` package is the standard factory for producing it. `clientcmd` handles the\n11: complex logic of parsing `kubeconfig` files, merging contexts, and handling external\n12: authentication providers (e.g., OIDC).\n13: \n14: ## REST Client\n15: \n16: The `rest.Client` is the foundational HTTP client that underpins all other clients. It separates\n17: the low-level concerns of HTTP transport, serialization, and error handling from higher-level,\n18: Kubernetes-specific object logic.\n19: \n20: The `rest.Config` object is used to build the underlying HTTP transport, which is typically a\n21: chain of `http.RoundTripper` objects. This is the mechanism by which all authentication\n23: is injected into requests.\n24: \n25: The client uses a builder pattern for requests (e.g., `.Verb()`, `.Resource()`), deferring\n26: response processing until a method like `.Into(&pod)` is called. This separation is key to\n27: supporting different client models from a common base.\n28: \n29: ### Endpoint Interactions\n30: \n31: *   **Content Negotiation:** The client uses HTTP `Accept` headers to negotiate the wire format\n32:     (JSON or Protobuf). A key performance optimization using this mechanism is the ability to\n33:     request metadata-only objects via the `as=PartialObjectMetadata;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameter.\n34:     Also the `as=Table;g=meta.k8s.io;v=v1` Accept custom parameters may be used to request lists as tables. \n35: *   **Subresources:** The client can target standard subresources like `/status` or `/scale` for\n36:     object mutations, and it can also handle action-oriented subresources like `/logs` or\n37:     `/exec`, which often involve streaming data.\n38: *   **List Pagination:** For `LIST` requests, the client can specify a `limit`. The server will\n39:     return up to that many items and, if more exist, a `continue` token. The client is\n40:     responsible for passing this token in a subsequent request to retrieve the next page.\n41:     Higher-level tools like the `Reflector`'s `ListerWatcher` handle this logic automatically.\n42: *   **Streaming Watches:** A `WATCH` request returns a `watch.Interface` (from\n43:     `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/watch`), which provides a channel of structured `watch.Event`\n44:     objects (`ADDED`, `MODIFIED`, `DELETED`, `BOOKMARK`). This decouples the watch consumer from\n45:     the underlying streaming protocol.\n46: \n47: ### Errors, Warnings, and Rate Limiting\n48: \n49: *   **Structured Errors:** The client deserializes non-2xx responses into a structured\n50:     `errors.StatusError`, enabling programmatic error handling (e.g., `errors.IsNotFound(err)`).\n51: *   **Warnings:** It processes non-fatal `Warning` headers from the API server via a\n52:     `WarningHandler`.\n53: *   **Client-Side Rate Limiting:** The `QPS` and `Burst` settings in `rest.Config` are the\n54:     client's half of the contract with the server's API Priority and Fairness system.\n55: *   **Server-Side Throttling:** The client's default transport automatically handles HTTP `429`\n56:     responses by reading the `Retry-After` header, waiting, and retrying the request.\n57: \n58: ## Typed and Dynamic Clients\n59: \n60: To handle the extensible nature of the Kubernetes API, `client-go` provides two primary client\n61: models.\n62: \n63: The **`kubernetes.Clientset`** provides compile-time, type-safe access to core, built-in APIs.\n64: \n65: The **`dynamic.DynamicClient`** represents all objects as `unstructured.Unstructured`, allowing it\n66: to interact with any API resource, including CRDs. It relies on two discovery mechanisms:\n67: 1.  The **`discovery.DiscoveryClient`** determines *what* resources exist. The\n68:     **`CachedDiscoveryClient`** is an optimization that caches this data on disk to solve.\n69: 2.  The **OpenAPI schema** (fetched from `/openapi/v3`) describes the *structure* of those\n70:     resources, providing the schema awareness needed by the dynamic client.\n71: \n72: ## Code Generation\n73: \n74: A core architectural principle of `client-go` is the use of code generation to provide a\n75: strongly-typed, compile-time-safe interface for specific API GroupVersions. This makes\n76: controller code more robust and easier to maintain. The tools in `k8s.io/code-generator` produce\n77: several key components:\n78: \n79: *   **Typed Clientsets:** The primary interface for interacting with a specific GroupVersion.\n80: *   **Typed Listers:** The read-only, cached accessors used by controllers.\n81: *   **Typed Informers:** The machinery for populating the cache for a specific type.\n82: *   **Apply Configurations:** The type-safe builders for Server-Side Apply.\n83: \n84: A contributor modifying a built-in API type **must** run the code generation scripts to update all\n85: of these dependent components. For the Kubernetes project, `hack/update-codegen.sh` runs code generation.\n86: \n87: `sample-controller` shows how code generate can be configured to build custom controllers.\n88: \n89: ## Controller Infrastructure\n90: \n91: The `tools/cache` package provides the core infrastructure for controllers, replacing a high-load,\n92: request-based pattern with a low-load, event-driven, cached model.\n93: \n94: The data flow is as follows:\n95: \n96: ```mermaid\n97: graph TD\n98:     subgraph \"Kubernetes API\"\n99:         API_Server[API Server]\n100:     end\n101: \n102:     subgraph \"client-go: Informer Mechanism\"\n103:         Reflector(\"1. Reflector\")\n104:         DeltaFIFO(\"2. DeltaFIFO\")\n105:         Indexer[\"3. Indexer (Cache)\"]\n106:         EventHandlers(\"4. Event Handlers\")\n107:     end\n108: \n109:     subgraph \"User Code\"\n110:         WorkQueue[\"5. Work Queue\"]\n111:         Controller(\"6. Controller\")\n112:     end\n113: \n114:     API_Server -- LIST/WATCH --> Reflector\n115:     Reflector -- Puts changes into --> DeltaFIFO\n116:     DeltaFIFO -- Is popped by internal loop, which updates --> Indexer\n117:     Indexer -- Update triggers --> EventHandlers\n118:     EventHandlers -- Adds key to --> WorkQueue\n119:     WorkQueue -- Is processed by --> Controller\n120:     Controller -- Reads from cache via Lister --> Indexer\n121: ```\n122: \n123: A **`Reflector`** performs a `LIST` to get a consistent snapshot of a resource, identified by a\n124: `resourceVersion`. It then starts a `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion` to receive a continuous\n125: stream of subsequent changes. The `Reflector`'s relist/rewatch loop is designed to solve the\n126: **\"too old\" `resourceVersion` error** by re-listing. To make this recovery more efficient, the\n127: `Reflector` consumes **watch bookmarks** from the server, which provide a more recent\n128: `resourceVersion` to restart from.\n129: \n130: The **`Lister`** is the primary, read-only, thread-safe interface for a controller's business\n131: logic to access the `Indexer`'s cache.\n132: \n133: ## Controller Patterns\n134: \n135: The controller infrastructure is architecturally decoupled from the controller's business logic to\n136: ensure resiliency.\n137: \n138: The **`util/workqueue`** creates a critical boundary between event detection (the informer's job)\n139: and reconciliation (the controller's job). Informer event handlers only add an object's key to the\n140: work queue. This allows the controller to retry failed operations with exponential backoff without\n141: blocking the informer's watch stream.\n142: \n143: For high availability, the **`tools/leaderelection`** package provides the standard architectural\n144: solution to ensure single-writer semantics by having replicas compete to acquire a lock on a\n145: shared `Lease` object.\n146: \n147: ## Server-Side Apply\n148: \n149: `client-go` provides a distinct architectural pattern for object mutation that aligns with the\n150: server's declarative model. This is a separate workflow from the traditional `get-modify-update`\n151: model that allows multiple controllers to safely co-manage the same object. The\n152: **`applyconfigurations`** package provides the generated, type-safe builder API used to\n153: construct the declarative patch.\n154: \n155: ## Versioning and Compatibility\n156: \n157: `client-go` has a strict versioning relationship with the main Kubernetes repository. A `client-go`\n158: version `v0.X.Y` corresponds to the Kubernetes version `v1.X.Y`.\n159: \n160: The Kubernetes API has strong backward compatibility guarantees: a client built with an older\n161: version of `client-go` will work with a newer API server. However, the reverse is not guaranteed.\n162: A contributor must not break compatibility with supported versions of the Kubernetes API server.\n163: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/ARCHITECTURE.md"}}}

An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n44: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n45: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n46: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n47: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n48: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n49: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n50: //\\n51: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n52: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n53: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n54: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n55: //\\n56: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n57: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n58: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n59: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n60: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n61: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n62: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n63: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n64: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n65: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n66: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n67: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n68: // selector.\\n69: //\\n70: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n71: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n72: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n73: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n74: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n75: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n76: //\\n77: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n78: // during `Run()`.\\n79: //\\n80: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n81: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n82: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n83: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n84: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n85: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n86: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n87: //\\n88: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n89: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n90: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n91: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n92: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n93: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n94: //\\n95: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n96: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n97: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n98: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n99: // into its constituent parts.\\n100: //\\n101: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n102: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n103: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n104: //\\n105: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n106: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n107: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n108: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n109: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n110: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n111: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n112: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n113: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n114: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n115: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n116: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n117: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n118: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n119: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n120: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n121: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n122: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n123: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n124: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n125: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n126: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n127: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n128: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n129: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n130: //\\n131: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n132: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n133: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n134: // to something else, for example through a\\n135: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n136: //\\n137: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n138: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n139: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n140: type SharedInformer interface {\\n141: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n142: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n143: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n144: \\t// different handlers.\\n145: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n146: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n147: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n148: \\t//\\n149: \\t// Contextual logging: AddEventHandlerWithOptions together with a logger in the options should be used instead of AddEventHandler in code which supports contextual logging.\\n150: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n151: One is that the\\n64: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n65: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n66: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n67: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n68: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n69: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n70: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n71: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n72: //\\n73: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n74: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n75: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n76: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n77: // resync events.\\n78: //\\n79: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n80: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n81: // the Pop() method.\\n82: //\\n83: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n84: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n85: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n86: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n87: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n88: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n89: //\\n90: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n91: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n92: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\\n93: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\\n94: //\\n95: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\\n96: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key. way).\\n100: //\\n101: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\\n102: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\\n103: // different versions of All are\n32: // optional.\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n34: \n35: \t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n36: \t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n37: \t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n38: \t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n39: \tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n40: \n41: \t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n42: \t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n43: \t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n44: \t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n45: \tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n46: \n47: \t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n48: \t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n49: \t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n50: \t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n51: \t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n52: \t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n53: \tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n54: \n55: \t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n56: \t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n57: \tTransformer TransformFunc\n58: \n59: \t// If set, log output will go to this logger instead of klog.Background().\n60: \tLogger *klog.Logger\n61: }\n62: \n63: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n64: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n65: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n66: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n67: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n68: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n69: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n70: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n71: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n72: //\n73: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n74: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n75: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n76: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n77: // resync events.\n78: //\n79: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n80: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n81: // the Pop() method.\n82: //\n83: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n84: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n85: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n86: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n87: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n88: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n89: //\n90: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n91: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n92: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n93: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n94: //\n95: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n96: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n97: // question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n98: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n99: // (each in a different way).\n100: //\n101: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n102: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n103: // different versions of the same object.\n104: type DeltaFIFO struct {\n105: \t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n106: \tlock sync.RWMutex\n107: \tcond sync.Cond\n108: \n109: \t// `items` maps a key to a Replace()\n122: \tinitialPopulationCount int\n123: \n124: \t// keyFunc is used to make the key used for queued item\n125: \t// insertion and retrieval, and should be deterministic.\n126: \tkeyFunc queue is closed so a control loop can exit when a queue is empty.\n133: \t// Currently, not used to gate any of CRUD operations.\n134: \tclosed bool\n135: \n136: \t// emitDeltaTypeReplaced is whether The error returned in 'err' must satisfy the\n93: \t// following conditions:\n94: \t//  a: errors.Unwrap(err) = errors.Unwrap(finalErr) if finalErr\n95: \t//     implements Unwrap\n96: \t//  b: errors.Unwrap(err) = finalErr if finalErr does not\n97: \t//     implements Unwrap\n98: \t//  c: errors.Is(err, otherErr) = errors.Is(finalErr, otherErr)\n99: \tWrapPreviousError(finalErr error) (err error)\n100: }\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/rest/with_retry.go%3FL1-100"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01HvAK3rQUi7uAeMCR3s2M6K","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01AW734pdXWgUG6SMJoxa658","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes Client-Go Systems Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nClient-go is the canonical Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It provides a complete abstraction layer between applications and the Kubernetes API server, handling HTTP transport, serialization, authentication, discovery, caching, and controller patterns. The library decouples request construction from response processing, uses code generation to provide compile-time type safety, and implements a sophisticated event-driven caching system for efficient resource monitoring.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nClient-go serves as the foundational client library for any Go application that needs to interact with Kubernetes APIs. It abstracts away HTTP mechanics, authentication complexity, and API conventions, providing both strongly-typed and dynamic interfaces to the API server.\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**What client-go owns:**\n- HTTP transport configuration and request/response handling (`rest/` package)\n- Configuration loading from kubeconfig files (`tools/clientcmd/`)\n- API discovery (determining what resources exist and their versions)\n- Typed, generated clients for built-in API groups (`kubernetes/` package)\n- Dynamic clients for unstructured data and Custom Resources (`dynamic/` package)\n- Controller infrastructure: list/watch sources, caching, event distribution (`tools/cache/`)\n- Work queue patterns for asynchronous reconciliation (`util/workqueue/`)\n- Leader election for high-availability controllers (`tools/leaderelection/`)\n- Server-side apply mechanics (`applyconfigurations/` package)\n\n**What client-go does NOT own:**\n- Controller reconciliation logic (user code responsibility)\n- Admission control or API server logic\n- Kubernetes cluster operations or scheduler behavior\n- Resource quotas or limit enforcement\n- Authentication/authorization policy definition\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n- **`k8s.io/apimachinery`**: Core Kubernetes types, watch mechanisms, serialization, runtime object handling\n- **`k8s.io/api`**: Typed definitions for core API groups (apps, batch, core, etc.)\n- **`k8s.io/code-generator`**: Code generation tools for typed clients, listers, and informers\n- **`k8s.io/klog`**: Structured logging\n\n### Downstream Dependents\n\n- **Controllers**: Any reconciliation loop (Kubernetes controllers, operators, webhooks)\n- **CLI tools**: kubectl, kube-proxy, kubelet all use client-go\n- **Operators**: Custom controllers managing application deployments\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### Component Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                      User Application                        │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│  Typed Clients (kubernetes.Clientset) | Dynamic Client     │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│  Informers & Listers | Work Queues | Leader Election       │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│  Cache (DeltaFIFO, Indexer) | Reflector                    │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│  REST Client | Discovery Client                            │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│  HTTP Transport | Auth | Serialization | Retry/Backoff     │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│            Configuration (kubeconfig, in-cluster)           │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n### Core Components\n\n#### 2.1 Configuration Management (`rest/config.go`, `tools/clientcmd/`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Load and merge kubeconfig files, apply command-line overrides, configure authentication and TLS.\n\n**Key types**:\n- `rest.Config`: In-memory representation of client configuration (host, auth credentials, TLS settings, QPS, burst)\n- `clientcmd.ClientConfig`: Interface for loading and resolving kubeconfig contexts\n\n**Critical fields in `rest.Config`**:\n- `Host`: API server endpoint\n- `BearerToken`, `BearerTokenFile`: Token authentication\n- `Username`, `Password`: Basic auth\n- `ExecProvider`, `AuthProvider`: Plugin-based authentication\n- `QPS`, `Burst`: Client-side rate limiting parameters\n- `TLSClientConfig`: Certificate-based authentication\n\n**Design decision**: Configuration loading is separate from client initialization. This allows multiple clients to share a single `Config` object, reducing resource overhead.\n\n#### 2.2 REST Client (`rest/client.go`, `rest/request.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Build and execute HTTP requests against the API server with proper serialization, error handling, and rate limiting.\n\n**Key types**:\n- `RESTClient`: Low-level HTTP client that enforces Kubernetes API conventions\n- `Request`: Builder pattern object for constructing requests\n\n**Request builder chain** (`rest/request.go:96-131`):\n```go\ntype Request struct {\n    verb           string          // GET, POST, PUT, DELETE, PATCH, WATCH\n    pathPrefix     string          // /api or /apis\n    resource       string          // pods, deployments, etc.\n    resourceName   string          // specific object name\n    namespace      string          // target namespace\n    subresource    string          // status, scale, log, exec\n    params         url.Values      // query parameters\n    headers        http.Header     // custom headers\n    body           io.Reader       // request body\n    // ... rate limiter, backoff, timeout, max retries\n}\n```\n\n**Design pattern**: Deferred execution. The builder is constructed incrementally, but the HTTP request is not sent until a terminal method like `.Into(&obj)` or `.Do()` is called. This allows different client types (typed, dynamic, discovery) to be built on a common HTTP foundation.\n\n**Example flow**:\n```\nclient.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n↓\ntranslateGetOptions() constructs Query and Headers\n↓\nclient.Verb(\"GET\").Resource(\"pods\").Namespace(\"default\").Name(\"my-pod\").Do(ctx)\n↓\nBuildHTTPRequest() constructs *http.Request\n↓\nDoRaw() executes via http.Client.Do() and deserializes response\n```\n\n#### 2.3 HTTP Transport and Authentication (`rest/transport.go`, `transport/` package)\n\n**Responsibility**: Wire up HTTP transport with authentication middleware, TLS configuration, and request/response hooks.\n\n**Middleware chain** (roundtrippers are composed):\n1. Custom user-provided roundtrippers (via `WrapTransport`)\n2. Bearer token injection\n3. Basic auth or Impersonation\n4. Client certificates / TLS\n5. User-Agent header injection\n6. Compression handling\n7. Retry/backoff for transient failures\n\n**Key design**: Each authentication method is implemented as an `http.RoundTripper` that wraps the underlying transport. This keeps concerns modular and composable.\n\n#### 2.4 Discovery Client (`discovery/discovery_client.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Query the API server to determine what API groups, versions, and resources exist.\n\n**Key interfaces**:\n- `DiscoveryInterface`: Methods to fetch API groups (`ServerGroups()`) and resources (`ServerResources()`)\n- `CachedDiscoveryClient`: Wraps DiscoveryClient and caches results to disk (typically `~/.kube/cache/`)\n\n**How discovery works** (`discovery/discovery_client.go:49-71`):\n- `/api/v1` (legacy core API)\n- `/apis` (aggregated API group discovery)\n- `/apis/{group}/{version}` (resources in a specific version)\n- `/openapi/v3` (OpenAPI schema for structural information)\n\n**Design rationale**: Caching discovery results dramatically reduces API server load. Clients cache on disk and only refresh on explicit invalidation or TTL expiry.\n\n#### 2.5 Typed Clients (`kubernetes/clientset.go`, `kubernetes/typed/`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Provide compile-time type-safe access to core API resources (Pods, Deployments, Services, etc.).\n\n**Structure** (`kubernetes/clientset.go:140-150`):\n```go\ntype Clientset struct {\n    *discovery.DiscoveryClient\n    appsV1         *appsv1.AppsV1Client\n    batchV1        *batchv1.BatchV1Client\n    corev1         *corev1.CoreV1Client\n    // ... one client per API group version\n}\n```\n\n**Generated interfaces** (via `k8s.io/code-generator`):\n```go\n// Example: corev1.PodsGetter generates:\ntype PodsGetter interface {\n    Pods(namespace string) PodInterface\n}\n\ntype PodInterface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, ...) (*v1.Pod, error)\n    Update(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, ...) (*v1.Pod, error)\n    Delete(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) error\n    Get(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) (*v1.Pod, error)\n    List(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (*v1.PodList, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n    // ... Patch, UpdateStatus, etc.\n}\n```\n\n**Code generation**: These clients are not hand-written. Running `k8s.io/code-generator` on API type definitions automatically produces:\n- CRUD client methods\n- Listers (cached, read-only accessors)\n- Informers (watch + cache machinery)\n- Apply configuration builders (server-side apply)\n\nThis ensures type safety while avoiding massive boilerplate.\n\n#### 2.6 Dynamic Client (`dynamic/interface.go`, `dynamic/simple.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Provide untyped, runtime-safe access to any API resource (core, CRDs, aggregated APIs).\n\n**Key interface** (`dynamic/interface.go:29-50`):\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Resource(resource schema.GroupVersionResource) NamespaceableResourceInterface\n}\n\ntype ResourceInterface interface {\n    Create(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Update(ctx context.Context, obj *unstructured.Unstructured, ...) (*unstructured.Unstructured, error)\n    Delete(ctx context.Context, name string, ...) error\n    List(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (*unstructured.UnstructuredList, error)\n    Watch(ctx context.Context, opts metav1.ListOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n    // ... Patch, Apply, etc.\n}\n```\n\n**Data representation**: All objects are `*unstructured.Unstructured`, which is a generic map-like structure containing raw JSON/CBOR data. The dynamic client relies on discovery to determine what API paths exist.\n\n**When to use**:\n- Working with CustomResourceDefinitions\n- Building generic tools (e.g., kubectl)\n- Handling resources not known at compile time\n\n**Tradeoff**: No compile-time type checking, but maximum flexibility.\n\n#### 2.7 Informers and Caching (`tools/cache/`, `informers/`)\n\n**Purpose**: Maintain an in-memory cache of API objects and notify handlers when objects change.\n\n**Core components**:\n\n##### Reflector (`tools/cache/reflector.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Perform a LIST to get initial state, then WATCH for incremental updates.\n\n**Algorithm** (`tools/cache/reflector.go:200-350`):\n1. Execute `LIST` with `limit` and get objects + `resourceVersion`\n2. Start `WATCH` from that `resourceVersion`\n3. Stream watch events into the store\n4. On `WATCH` error or \"too old resourceVersion\":\n   - If error was \"resourceVersion too old\": use watch bookmarks to get fresher resourceVersion\n   - Exponential backoff (max 30s) before retry\n   - Exponential backoff resets if no error for 2 minutes\n\n**Key parameters** (`tools/cache/reflector.go:228-251`):\n```go\ntype ReflectorOptions struct {\n    Name            string              // For logging\n    ResyncPeriod    time.Duration       // Force refresh all cached objects\n    MinWatchTimeout time.Duration       // Minimum timeout for WATCH requests\n    Clock           clock.Clock         // For testing\n}\n```\n\n**Why the resync period?** Even if the WATCH stream is healthy, the cache may have drifted due to bugs or missed events. Periodic resync forces re-processing of all cached objects.\n\n##### DeltaFIFO (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Queue and accumulate changes (deltas) for each object.\n\n**Data model** (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go:63-99`):\n```go\ntype Deltas []Delta\ntype Delta struct {\n    Type   DeltaType  // Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync, Replaced\n    Object interface{} // The actual Kubernetes object\n}\n```\n\n**Why deltas?** Controllers need to see the full sequence of changes to an object, not just its current state. DeltaFIFO queues are keyed by object name, so multiple changes to the same object before it's processed are coalesced into a Deltas slice.\n\n**Example**:\n- Object created: Queue contains `[{Added, Pod(v1)}]`\n- Object modified 3 times: Queue still contains key once, but Deltas = `[{Added, Pod(v1)}, {Updated, Pod(v2)}, {Updated, Pod(v3)}]`\n- Object deleted: Queue contains `[{Deleted, Pod(v3)}]`\n\n##### Indexer and ThreadSafeStore (`tools/cache/index.go`, `tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Store cached objects, provide thread-safe access, and support secondary indexes for fast lookups.\n\n**Indexing example**:\n```go\n// NamespaceIndex: index objects by namespace\nIndexers{\n    NamespaceIndex: func(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {\n        meta, _ := meta.Accessor(obj)\n        return []string{meta.GetNamespace()}, nil\n    },\n}\n```\n\n**Why indexing?** Controllers often need to list all objects in a namespace or with a certain label. Indexes provide O(1) lookup instead of O(n) full scans.\n\n##### SharedInformer (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Orchestrate Reflector, DeltaFIFO, and Indexer; dispatch events to multiple handlers.\n\n**Key contract** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go:41-102`):\n- Cache is **eventually consistent** with the API server\n- Notifications are ordered per-object but not cross-object\n- Handlers are called **after** cache updates\n- Handlers must process quickly (use workqueue for heavy lifting)\n\n**Handler registration**:\n```go\ninformer.AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) { /* new object */ },\n    UpdateFunc: func(oldObj, newObj interface{}) { /* changed */ },\n    DeleteFunc: func(obj interface{}) { /* removed */ },\n})\n```\n\n**Design pattern**: Multiple controllers can register handlers on the same informer. The informer deduplicates LIST/WATCH requests to the API server, reducing load.\n\n#### 2.8 Informer Factory (`informers/factory.go`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Create and manage a set of SharedInformers for all API types, with a unified lifecycle.\n\n**Key options** (`informers/factory.go:54-109`):\n```go\ntype SharedInformerOption func(*sharedInformerFactory)\n\n// WithCustomResyncConfig: different resync periods for different types\nWithCustomResyncConfig(map[v1.Object]time.Duration)\n\n// WithTweakListOptions: filter cached objects (e.g., single namespace)\nWithTweakListOptions(func(*metav1.ListOptions))\n\n// WithNamespace: limit to one namespace\nWithNamespace(namespace string)\n\n// WithTransform: transform cached objects before storing (e.g., strip secrets)\nWithTransform(cache.TransformFunc)\n```\n\n**Lifecycle**:\n```go\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions(clientset, 10*time.Second)\npodInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\nfactory.Start(stopCh)        // Start all informers\nfactory.WaitForCacheSync(stopCh) // Wait for initial LIST\n// Now podInformer.Lister().Pods(ns).List() is safe\nfactory.Shutdown()           // Stop all informers\n```\n\n#### 2.9 Work Queue (`util/workqueue/`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Decouple event detection (informers) from reconciliation (controller logic).\n\n**Queue properties** (`util/workqueue/doc.go`):\n- **Fair**: Items processed in order\n- **Stingy**: No concurrent processing of the same item\n- **Durable**: Item stays in queue until explicitly marked done\n- **Retryable**: Failed items can be re-queued with backoff\n\n**Rate limiting strategies** (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`):\n```go\n// Linear backoff: 1x, 2x, 3x, ..., capped at maxRetries\nNewItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(1*time.Second, 1*time.Hour)\n\n// Exponential backoff: 2^n\nNewMaxOfRateLimiter(exponential, linear, baseDelay)\n```\n\n**Typical controller loop**:\n```go\nfor {\n    item, shutdown := queue.Get()\n    if shutdown { break }\n\n    err := r.reconcile(item.(string))\n    if err != nil {\n        queue.AddRateLimited(item) // Retry with backoff\n    } else {\n        queue.Forget(item) // Reset backoff counter\n    }\n    queue.Done(item)\n}\n```\n\n#### 2.10 Leader Election (`tools/leaderelection/`)\n\n**Responsibility**: Coordinate multiple replicas of a controller, ensuring only one is active.\n\n**Mechanism**:\n- Replicas compete to acquire a `Lease` object\n- Holder periodically updates the lease\n- Other replicas watch the lease, take over if holder dies\n- Graceful shutdown releases the lease\n\n**Configuration**:\n```go\nleaderelection.LeaderElect(context.Background(), leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{\n    Lock: &resourcelock.LeaseLock{\n        Client: clientset.CoordinationV1(),\n        LockConfig: resourcelock.ResourceLockConfig{\n            Identity: hostname,\n        },\n    },\n    LeaseDuration: 15 * time.Second,\n    RenewDeadline: 10 * time.Second,\n    RetryPeriod:   2 * time.Second,\n    Callbacks: leaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{\n        OnStartedLeading: func(ctx context.Context) { /* become active */ },\n        OnStoppedLeading: func() { /* stop reconciling */ },\n    },\n})\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### Scenario 1: Watching a Pod\n\n**User code**:\n```go\nconfig, _ := clientcmd.BuildConfigFromFlags(\"\", os.ExpandEnv(\"$HOME/.kube/config\"))\nclientset, _ := kubernetes.NewForConfig(config)\nwatch, _ := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Watch(ctx, metav1.ListOptions{})\n\nfor event := range watch.ResultChan() {\n    pod := event.Object.(*v1.Pod)\n    fmt.Printf(\"%s: %s\\n\", event.Type, pod.Name)\n}\n```\n\n**Internal flow**:\n\n1. **Config loading** (`tools/clientcmd/loader.go`):\n   - Parse kubeconfig file (default: `~/.kube/config`)\n   - Resolve context, cluster, user\n   - Load certificates/tokens\n   - Return `rest.Config`\n\n2. **Transport creation** (`rest/transport.go`):\n   - Build TLS config from certificates\n   - Stack roundtrippers: auth, compression, user-agent, retry\n   - Create `http.Client`\n\n3. **Clientset creation** (`kubernetes/clientset.go`):\n   - Create RESTClient for each API group\n   - Each client wraps the shared transport\n\n4. **Watch request** (`rest/request.go:Verb`, `rest/client.go:Watch`):\n   - `client.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Watch()` → `Request.Verb(\"WATCH\")`\n   - Build URL: `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods?watch=true`\n   - Set headers: `Accept: application/json`\n   - Call `Do()` → `client.Do(req)` (executes HTTP)\n\n5. **Stream handling** (`rest/request.go:Stream`):\n   - HTTP response is streamed (not fully buffered)\n   - Decoder reads `watch.Event` objects from stream\n   - Each event is wrapped in a `watch.RawEvent`\n\n6. **Response decoding** (`k8s.io/apimachinery`):\n   - Each line is a JSON-encoded `metav1.WatchEvent`\n   - Deserialize object field into `v1.Pod`\n   - Pass to user's `ResultChan()`\n\n**Evidence from code**:\n- `rest/request.go:Do()` orchestrates the request\n- `rest/request.go:Stream()` returns `io.ReadCloser`\n- `rest/watch/decoder.go` (in apimachinery) decodes streaming watch events\n\n### Scenario 2: Informer-Based Cache Population\n\n**User code**:\n```go\nfactory := informers.NewSharedInformerFactory(clientset, 10*time.Second)\npodInformer := factory.Core().V1().Pods()\n\npodInformer.Informer().AddEventHandler(cache.ResourceEventHandlerFuncs{\n    AddFunc: func(obj interface{}) {\n        pod := obj.(*v1.Pod)\n        queue.Add(pod.Namespace + \"/\" + pod.Name)\n    },\n})\n\nfactory.Start(stopCh)\nfactory.WaitForCacheSync(stopCh)\n\npods, _ := podInformer.Lister().List(labels.Everything())\n```\n\n**Internal flow**:\n\n1. **Factory initialization** (`informers/factory.go:125-142`):\n   - Create map to track informers (one per type)\n   - Store options (namespace filter, custom resync, transform)\n\n2. **Informer creation** (on first access to `.Pods()`):\n   - Create `SharedIndexInformer` for `v1.Pod`\n   - Create `Reflector` with ListerWatcher\n   - Create `DeltaFIFO` with `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc` and known objects\n   - Create Indexer for namespace indexing\n   - Wire up event handlers\n\n3. **Start** (`informers/factory.go:144-170`):\n   - For each informer, spawn goroutine running `reflector.Run()`\n   - For each informer, spawn goroutine running `informer.processLoop()` (pops from DeltaFIFO)\n\n4. **Reflector LIST phase** (`tools/cache/reflector.go:150-190`):\n   - Call `listerWatcher.List()` → REST client → HTTP GET `/api/v1/pods`\n   - Receive `PodList` object\n   - Extract ResourceVersion from list metadata\n   - Call `store.Replace(items, rv)` → DeltaFIFO queues \"Replaced\" deltas\n\n5. **Reflector WATCH phase** (`tools/cache/reflector.go:190-200`):\n   - Call `listerWatcher.Watch()` → HTTP GET with `?watch=true&resourceVersion=<rv>`\n   - Stream watch events into `store.Update()` / `store.Add()` / `store.Delete()`\n\n6. **DeltaFIFO processing** (`tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`):\n   - Internal goroutine pops from queue\n   - For each delta, call `store.Update()` on the Indexer\n   - Trigger event handlers (Add/Update/Delete)\n\n7. **Handler invocation** (`tools/cache/shared_informer.go`):\n   - Each registered handler is called in sequence\n   - Handler calls `queue.Add(key)` (e.g., \"default/my-pod\")\n\n8. **Lister access**:\n   - `podInformer.Lister()` returns read-only interface to Indexer\n   - `.List(labels.Everything())` returns all cached pods\n   - `.Get(\"my-pod\")` does O(1) lookup in indexer\n\n**Evidence from code**:\n- `tools/cache/reflector.go:ListWatch()` implements the LIST-WATCH pattern\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:Run()` orchestrates all components\n- `informers/factory.go:Start()` starts all informers\n- Handlers are called from `tools/cache/controller.go:processLoop()`\n\n### Scenario 3: Request with Retry and Backoff\n\n**User code**:\n```go\npod, err := clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-pod\", metav1.GetOptions{})\n```\n\n**Internal flow on server error**:\n\n1. **Request construction** (`rest/request.go`):\n   - Build GET request to `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/my-pod`\n   - Set max retries (default 0 for GET)\n\n2. **Rate limiting** (`rest/request.go:Do`):\n   - Acquire token from rate limiter (based on QPS/Burst in Config)\n   - Log if throttled > 50ms\n\n3. **Backoff and retry** (`rest/with_retry.go`):\n   - If response is 429 or 5xx with Retry-After header:\n     - Read `Retry-After` value\n     - Sleep for duration\n     - Retry request\n   - If `context.DeadlineExceeded` or transient error:\n     - Backoff timer increments exponentially\n     - Retry until max retries exceeded\n\n4. **Error deserialization** (`rest/request.go:Into`):\n   - If status >= 400:\n     - Decode response body as `metav1.Status`\n     - Return `errors.StatusError` (has `Status()` method)\n     - User can call `errors.IsNotFound(err)`, `errors.IsConflict(err)`, etc.\n\n**Evidence from code**:\n- `rest/request.go:106-107` define `maxRetries` and `timeout`\n- `rest/request.go:Do()` calls `retry.IsNextRetry()` loop\n- `rest/request.go:transformUnstructuredError()` handles error responses\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Failure Mode 1: API Server Unavailability\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Reflector detects WATCH stream closure\n- Exponential backoff kicks in (starts at 800ms, capped at 30s)\n- After 2 minutes without errors, backoff resets\n- Informer cache becomes stale but still serves requests\n\n**Risk**: Controllers may reconcile based on outdated state. Mitigation: periodic resync forces re-processing of all objects.\n\n**Evidence**: `tools/cache/reflector.go:282-283`\n\n### Failure Mode 2: \"resourceVersion too old\"\n\n**Cause**: API server garbage-collects old revisions (default 5 minutes). If WATCH reconnects after that period, the requested `resourceVersion` no longer exists.\n\n**Behavior**:\n1. Error received from server\n2. Reflector detects error and falls back to LIST\n3. Exponential backoff before retrying\n4. Watch bookmarks (if enabled) provide fresher resourceVersion to resume from\n\n**Mitigation**: Increase `minWatchTimeout` to trigger more frequent bookmarks.\n\n**Evidence**: `tools/cache/reflector.go:268-270` (`defaultMinWatchTimeout = 5 * time.Minute`)\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Concurrent Handler Processing\n\n**Design tradeoff**: SharedInformer invokes event handlers **sequentially** for a given object, but different objects may be processed in parallel.\n\n**Risk**: If two handlers try to modify the same object, race conditions possible. Mitigation: Use work queues and atomic updates.\n\n**Evidence**: `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:118-120`\n\n### Failure Mode 4: Missing Delete Events\n\n**Cause**: Long watch streams can lose events if connection drops. Objects deleted during downtime appear as \"disappeared from cache\" without a DeleteFunc call.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Periodic resync (Reflector's `resyncPeriod`) compares cache against current API state\n- DeleteFunc is called for objects in cache but not in fresh LIST\n\n**Tradeoff**: Resync adds API server load but guarantees eventual consistency.\n\n### Failure Mode 5: Controller Deadlock\n\n**Risk**: If event handler is slow, event queue backs up and informer blocks trying to dispatch events.\n\n**Design**: Handler must be fast (< 100ms). Heavy work must be offloaded to work queue.\n\n**Evidence**: `tools/cache/shared_informer.go:131-135`\n\n### Failure Mode 6: Authentication Token Expiry\n\n**Behavior**:\n- Bearer token from ExecProvider is periodically refreshed\n- Stale token causes 401 response\n- Client retries with refreshed token\n\n**Tradeoff**: Adds latency to first request after token expiry.\n\n**Evidence**: `rest/plugin.go` (auth provider refresh logic)\n\n### Performance Limits\n\n| Aspect | Limit | Notes |\n|--------|-------|-------|\n| List pagination | Determined by server | Default 500 items per page |\n| Watch stream timeout | 5-10 minutes (random jitter) | Spreads load on API server |\n| Cache size | Limited by available memory | Typical: GB-scale for Kubernetes |\n| Resync period | 0 (disabled) to hours | Tradeoff: accuracy vs. load |\n| QPS limit | Client-side: 5.0 (default) | Server enforces API Priority & Fairness |\n| Burst | Client-side: 10 (default) | Allows bursts above QPS |\n| Informer propagation latency | <1s typical, <5s P99 | Depends on API server load |\n\n### Design Tradeoffs\n\n| Tradeoff | Choice | Rationale |\n|----------|--------|-----------|\n| **Cache consistency** | Eventual, not strong | Reduces latency and API server load |\n| **Request vs. streaming** | Separate HTTP stacks | Watch is streaming, GET is request/response |\n| **Retry logic** | Client-side only | Server does not know about retries |\n| **Code generation** | Required for typed clients | Ensures type safety but requires toolchain |\n| **Informer update ordering** | Per-object only | Cross-object ordering would require global coordination |\n| **Transport sharing** | Multiple clients share auth chain | Reduces redundant roundtrip middleware |\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### Extension Point 1: Authentication Plugins\n\n**Hook location**: `rest.Config.AuthProvider`, `rest.Config.ExecProvider`\n\n**Types**:\n- `AuthProvider`: OIDC, cloud-specific auth (GCP, AWS)\n- `ExecProvider`: Call external command for credentials (e.g., AWS IAM authenticator)\n\n**Implementation**: Plugins implement `AuthProviderConfigPersister` to update kubeconfig after refresh.\n\n**Risk**: Slow auth provider blocks all API requests. Mitigation: Refresh tokens in background, use timeouts.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nconfig.ExecProvider = &clientcmdapi.ExecConfig{\n    Command: \"aws-iam-authenticator\",\n    Args:    []string{\"token\", \"-i\", \"my-cluster\"},\n}\n```\n\n### Extension Point 2: Transport Wrapping\n\n**Hook location**: `rest.Config.WrapTransport`\n\n**Purpose**: Inject custom HTTP middleware (logging, metrics, custom headers).\n\n**Signature**:\n```go\ntype WrapTransportFunc func(http.RoundTripper) http.RoundTripper\n```\n\n**Example**: Log all requests\n```go\nconfig.WrapTransport = func(rt http.RoundTripper) http.RoundTripper {\n    return &LoggingRoundTripper{rt}\n}\n```\n\n**Risk**: Slow wrapper blocks all requests. Mitigation: Keep logic minimal, use buffering for metrics.\n\n### Extension Point 3: Informer Transformation\n\n**Hook location**: `informers.WithTransform(cache.TransformFunc)`\n\n**Purpose**: Modify cached objects before storing (e.g., redact secrets, normalize fields).\n\n**Signature**:\n```go\ntype TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\n```\n\n**Example**: Strip sensitive fields\n```go\ninformers.WithTransform(func(obj interface{}) (interface{}, error) {\n    secret := obj.(*v1.Secret)\n    secret.Data = nil // Redact\n    return secret, nil\n})\n```\n\n**Risk**: Invalid transformation corrupts cache. Mitigation: Return nil for unsupported types.\n\n### Extension Point 4: Reflector Watch Error Handling\n\n**Hook location**: `cache.Reflector.SetWatchErrorHandler()`\n\n**Purpose**: Custom handling of watch stream errors (e.g., metrics, alerting).\n\n**Signature**:\n```go\ntype WatchErrorHandler func(*Reflector, error)\n```\n\n**Risk**: Must not block for long. Mitigation: Async metrics/alerting.\n\n### Extension Point 5: Indexer Functions\n\n**Hook location**: `cache.NewIndexer(keyFunc, indexers)`\n\n**Purpose**: Define secondary indexes for fast lookups.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\nindexers := cache.Indexers{\n    \"ownerRef\": func(obj interface{}) ([]string, error) {\n        pod := obj.(*v1.Pod)\n        return pod.OwnerReferences[0].Name, nil\n    },\n}\nindexer := cache.NewIndexer(cache.MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, indexers)\n```\n\n**Risk**: Poorly designed index function is called for every object. Mitigation: Keep logic O(1).\n\n### Extension Point 6: Work Queue Rate Limiters\n\n**Hook location**: `workqueue.NewRateLimitingQueue(rateLimiter)`\n\n**Purpose**: Custom backoff strategies for failed items.\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype RateLimiter interface {\n    When(item interface{}) time.Duration\n    Forget(item interface{})\n    NumRequeues(item interface{}) int\n}\n```\n\n**Risk**: Runaway queue growth if rate limiter is too permissive. Mitigation: Monitor queue depth.\n\n### Extension Point 7: ClientConfig BuildRule Chain\n\n**Hook location**: `clientcmd.NewNonInteractiveDeferredLoadingClientConfig(loadingRules)`\n\n**Purpose**: Custom kubeconfig loading (e.g., from environment, ConfigMaps).\n\n**Signature**:\n```go\ntype KubeconfigGetter interface {\n    GetKubeconfig() *clientcmdapi.Config\n}\n```\n\n**Risk**: Invalid config blocks all clients. Mitigation: Validate config early.\n\n### Extension Point 8: REST Client Decorators\n\n**Hook location**: Multiple REST clients can be composed\n\n**Purpose**: Wrap a typed client to add caching, circuit breakers, etc.\n\n**Example**:\n```go\ntype CachingClient struct {\n    client kubernetes.Interface\n    cache  map[string]interface{}\n}\n\nfunc (c *CachingClient) CoreV1() corev1.CoreV1Interface {\n    return &CachingCoreV1{c.client.CoreV1(), c.cache}\n}\n```\n\n**Risk**: Cache invalidation is hard. Mitigation: Use informers for authoritative data.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Performance Considerations\n\n#### 6.1 Cache Memory Usage\n\n**Factor 1: Object size** — A `Pod` with many containers can be 100+ KB. A 10K-pod cluster needs several hundred MB in cache.\n\n**Factor 2: Garbage collection** — Large caches can trigger GC pauses. Mitigations:\n- Set memory limits on controller Pods\n- Use namespace-scoped informers when possible\n- Implement object size limits in transformers\n\n#### 6.2 API Server Load\n\n**LIST requests**: Full cluster state, can be slow. Mitigations:\n- Enable `Watch List` feature (WatchListClient gate) to combine LIST and WATCH\n- Use field selectors/label selectors to reduce scope\n- Configure higher `resyncPeriod` (e.g., 30 minutes) or disable resync entirely if eventual consistency is acceptable\n\n**WATCH streams**: Persistent connections consume socket/memory on server. Scale considerations:\n- 1000 controllers × 10 informers per controller = 10K concurrent WATCH streams\n- API server default `--max-requests-inflight=400` limits concurrent requests\n\n#### 6.3 Network Efficiency\n\n**Protocol optimization**:\n- Protobuf (if supported): 5-10x smaller than JSON\n- Gzip compression: Controlled by `DisableCompression` in Config\n- Chunked transfer encoding: For streaming watch events\n\n**Example**: To enable protobuf:\n```go\nconfig.ContentConfig.ContentType = \"application/vnd.kubernetes.protobuf\"\n```\n\n### Reliability Considerations\n\n#### 6.1 Timeouts\n\n**Client timeout** (`rest.Config.Timeout`):\n- Applies to each HTTP request roundtrip\n- Does NOT apply to long-lived streams (WATCH)\n- Default: 0 (no timeout)\n\n**Watch timeout**:\n- Server-enforced (typically 30-60s)\n- Client reconnects with new `resourceVersion`\n\n**Recommendation**:\n```go\nconfig.Timeout = 30 * time.Second // For non-watch requests\n```\n\n#### 6.2 Graceful Shutdown\n\n**Pattern**:\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\nfactory.Start(ctx.Done())\n// ... controller logic ...\ncancel() // Trigger shutdown\nfactory.Shutdown() // Wait for graceful termination\n```\n\n**Why explicit shutdown?** Informers hold open WATCH streams. Abrupt termination can leave orphaned connections on API server.\n\n#### 6.3 Circuit Breaker Pattern\n\n**Risk**: Cascading failures if controller hammers a degraded API server.\n\n**Mitigation**:\n```go\nqueue := workqueue.NewRateLimitingQueue(workqueue.NewMaxOfRateLimiter(\n    workqueue.NewItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(1*time.Second, 30*time.Second),\n    &workqueue.BucketRateLimiter{...},\n))\n```\n\n### Observability Considerations\n\n#### 6.1 Metrics Hooks\n\n**Available hooks**:\n- `tools/metrics`: Request latency, count by resource type\n- Workqueue metrics: Queue depth, latency, retries\n- Reflector metrics: List/watch latencies, errors\n\n**Integration example**:\n```go\nimport \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/metrics\"\n\nmetrics.Register() // Export Prometheus metrics\n```\n\n#### 6.2 Logging\n\n**Levels**:\n- V(0): Errors only\n- V(2): Informational (watch errors, resync events)\n- V(4): Debug (request details, auth refreshes)\n\n**Contextual logging** (with `klog`):\n```go\nlog := klog.FromContext(ctx)\nlog.V(2).Info(\"Watch started\", \"resource\", \"pods\")\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core REST Client\n- `rest/config.go` (145 lines): `Config` struct, default QPS/burst\n- `rest/client.go` (150+ lines): `RESTClient`, verb builder, constructor\n- `rest/request.go` (200+ lines): `Request` builder, `.Do()`, `.Into()`, error handling\n- `rest/transport.go` (100+ lines): HTTP transport, TLS, auth, roundtrippers\n- `rest/with_retry.go` (100+ lines): Retry semantics, exponential backoff\n\n### Configuration & Authentication\n- `tools/clientcmd/loader.go`: Load and parse kubeconfig files\n- `tools/clientcmd/client_config.go`: Merge contexts, resolve credentials\n- `tools/clientcmd/auth_loaders.go`: Load certificates, tokens, exec providers\n- `rest/plugin.go`: Authentication provider plugins (OIDC, cloud auth)\n\n### Discovery\n- `discovery/discovery_client.go` (100+ lines): Query API groups and resources\n- `discovery/cached/`: Disk-based discovery caching\n\n### Typed Clients (Generated)\n- `kubernetes/clientset.go` (150+ lines): Main Clientset interface and constructor\n- `kubernetes/typed/core/v1/pod.go`: Generated Pod client (interface + impl)\n- `kubernetes/typed/apps/v1/deployment.go`: Generated Deployment client\n\n### Dynamic Client\n- `dynamic/interface.go` (60+ lines): ResourceInterface for untyped objects\n- `dynamic/simple.go`: Concrete implementation using REST client\n\n### Informers & Caching\n- `tools/cache/reflector.go` (300+ lines): LIST-WATCH orchestration\n- `tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` (300+ lines): Delta accumulation queue\n- `tools/cache/shared_informer.go` (300+ lines): SharedInformer orchestration\n- `tools/cache/index.go` (150+ lines): Indexing and fast lookups\n- `tools/cache/store.go` (100+ lines): Interface definitions\n- `tools/cache/listwatch.go` (150+ lines): ListerWatcher interface\n\n### Informer Factory\n- `informers/factory.go` (200+ lines): SharedInformerFactory constructor and lifecycle\n- `informers/core/v1/pod.go`: Generated Pod informer factory\n- `informers/internalinterfaces/`: Shared interfaces for generated informers\n\n### Work Queue\n- `util/workqueue/queue.go` (150+ lines): Basic queue with deduplication\n- `util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go` (100+ lines): Rate limiting wrapper\n- `util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go` (100+ lines): Exponential backoff, token bucket\n\n### Leader Election\n- `tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go` (200+ lines): Main election loop\n- `tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/`: Lease-based lock implementations\n\n### Apply Configurations (Server-Side Apply)\n- `applyconfigurations/core/v1/pod.go`: Generated apply config builder\n- `util/apply/`: Core logic for SSA patches\n\n---\n\n## 8. Critical Design Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Builder Pattern for Requests\nEvery REST operation is constructed incrementally, deferring execution until `.Do()` or `.Into()` is called. This allows different client models to reuse the same HTTP infrastructure.\n\n### Pattern 2: Deferred Event Handling\nInformers queue changes into DeltaFIFO before invoking handlers. This creates a natural boundary where fast event dispatch (queue enqueue) is separated from slow handler logic.\n\n### Pattern 3: Exponential Backoff with Reset\nTransient failures trigger exponential backoff, but success resets the backoff timer. This prevents thundering herds on API server recovery.\n\n### Pattern 4: Lazy Initialization of Informers\nInformerFactory creates informers only on first access, reducing resource usage for unused API types.\n\n### Pattern 5: Composition Over Inheritance\nMultiple RoundTripper middleware (auth, compression, retry) are composed into a chain, avoiding deep inheritance hierarchies.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Conclusion\n\nClient-go is architected around a few core principles:\n\n1. **Separation of concerns**: Configuration loading, HTTP transport, API discovery, caching, and controller patterns are all decoupled.\n\n2. **Eventually consistent caching**: The Reflector continuously synchronizes cache with the API server, accepting brief periods of staleness for reduced load.\n\n3. **Code generation for type safety**: Typed clients and informers are generated, ensuring compile-time correctness.\n\n4. **Work queue pattern**: Controllers use queues to decouple event detection from reconciliation, enabling retries and prioritization.\n\n5. **Composable middleware**: HTTP behavior (auth, retry, compression) is stacked as RoundTripper middleware, allowing extensibility.\n\nThese patterns enable client-go to efficiently serve both low-latency (kubectl) and high-throughput (controllers) use cases while maintaining simplicity and testability. Understanding these patterns is essential for building reliable Kubernetes-native applications.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":314,"cache_read_input_tokens":82760,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":314},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2be44042-0639-40cf-99c5-188f09ad71df","uuid":"a249d334-a656-44ae-bc1f-343b4f3f843e"}
